Autotune is literally just another tool in any audio engineers abundance of tools, and people need to chill tf out about it  Literally 99.999% vocal parts in music you hear have compression and eq on them, yet no one tells vocalists they just need to get better at controlling their resonance and articulation/loudness.  I'm a deathcore/metalcore vocalist/singer, and tbh, my vocals would sound terrible without any mixing, but so do most other raw vocals, and refining them with digital tools is just as much a skill as doing vocals themselves. (Not to mention how many mixing plug-ins are also used for stylistic effects beyond their intended purpose, for example, autotune in t pains music or the exorbitant amount of guttural vocal compression in Hans Zimmers Dune Soundtrack.)  It's like saying a guitar player has no skill cause they use an Amp to achieve their sound.  In the end the only thing that matters is if people like the music, and if they do, an artist is most likely doing something that works for them and their audience.

Agree with all the T Pain commentary, love him, liked the video.  But, I have to disagree with your arguement that pitch is just as important as other factors.  Pitch is the foundation of good vocal singing.  You have to have pitch before any of the other factors matter.  You don't have to have perfect pitch, but if you don't have good pitch you don't sound pleasing to the ear as a singer. One comment can absolutely wreck a person for a long time.  When I finally decided to transition to male, one of the things I had never worried about "passing" with was my voice.  As a child I had such a low singing voice that I sang with the boys in the tenor section in choir despite being AFAB and - at that time - presenting female.  I've always been fairly good at manipulating my voice as well, and thought that it was overall neutral-sounding and could skew masculine or feminine as-wanted.  But one day on a Zoom voice call, someone I'd never met before greeted me with, "hello sir, how are you?" based on my masculine name.  In a masculine tone and pitch I felt confident in, I replied, "Great, how are you?" and her reaction was, and I quote, "Oh!  A woman!"  Now, this was a well-meaning stranger who had no idea what they'd just said might be upsetting to me at all, so clearly it's not the same.  And ftr, I know that logically, cismen get misgendered on the phone, too.  And no, I'm not overly sensitive to being misgendered - I have a thick skin.    My point is just that despite all this logic, those three words have stuck with me and I've been self-conscious about my voice ever since.  I can't imagine how much worse I would have felt if it had been from a friend who knew it would hurt me.  tl;dr the fact that you use your platform to encourage being a better person and let us all witness your personal growth as your audience slaps, because with a platform as large as yours, it's not just about you and what you believe in - you're cultivating that same mindset in millions of viewers.  That's damn good work worth doing, and I'm glad you exist.

really appreciate D'Angelo for actually giving facts. As a musician and sound technician I can confirm the plugin used for correcting notes is indeed melodyne, "auto-tune" is just the specific effect. Every studio artist today has their pitch corrected in melodyne and even in live performances the notes are flatlined, (you can put pitch correction in post) so basically whenever a microphone receives input this signal is transformed through the effect.  Pitch correcting is ok. There's still great singers that use pitch correction like Ariana Grande or Mariah Carey. Vocals aren't perfect and that's ok. It's ok to use pitch correction and it's ok not to, it will just sound more raw.

Just one point: comparing one similar instrument to another, like acoustic guitar vs. electric guitar, isn't quite the same as comparing an "acoustic" voice vs. an "edited" voice. The instruments are constructed very differently, and even if you wire and amplify an acoustic guitar, it's still going to sound like an acoustic guitar. So, natural vs. edited vocals sound very different and it's important to recognize it. Those who are striving to be Beyonce need to understand that, as amazing as she is, she has a unique instrument and ALSO benefits from vocal editing that cannot be reproduced

T pain can actually sing. There are plenty of videos of him doing it. I make and produce music, and I dont have an issue with pitch correction in moderation to improve albums...live I dunno how I feel about it. Pitch correction is usually considered different than autotune. Autotune is when you push pitch correction to it max and gives it that robotic flutter. When used as an effect to enhance a song, or just an effect I feel it's acceptable. If you're using it to try to hide your singing I'm not all that about it. Pitch correction is like a standard in music now and I'd bet money in a professional studio people like usher use it sparingly... most r&b, pop, rap, and even poppy emo bands use it. Basically any huge band you can think of use subtle pitch correction in a studio session, and also most times when you see people live dancing around ...yeah pitch correction. However people like t pain, and kanye used it as an effect. He did however popularize it at the time and people ran with it. Right now I'm at the point where you kind of point out what I'm saying and you mentioned melodyne. Another popular software for this is antares. Sorry to repeat some of what you said. I used to be this lofi indie surfy garage rock musician, and now I make beats, and house music. When I do vocals depending on the genre I will use extreme pitch correct as an effect. When you listen to my solo music I made as surfy garage rock indie surf artist I dont and I'm by no stretch of the imagination am a great singer but it suits the music. Just like when I use autotune as an effect for specific songs now ...its a tool. Instruments,mics, rack units, recorders, effects pedals.. they are all tools. I dont think people are really in a place to judge regarding this, and it's cool because as I'm typing this you're somewhat describing the history of it and what I said in the beginning its apparent you want to educate and you've done your research.

Sideways made a really good video about "auto-tune" in the industry
Since you mentioned guitars, a better comparison would be between fretless instruments like violins, violas, cellos, double basses, and ouds and fretted instruments like guitars, sitars, banjos, mandolins, and lutes. Our frets do "correct" our pitch so that we don't have to put our fingers in exactly the right spots every single time, which allows many of us to play chords (particularly with more intricate and complex rhythms). In a nutshell, frets opened up a whole new world of possibilities for stringed instruments that are wildly impractical (if not altogether impossible) on instruments without frets. SOME (but definitely not most) people who play fretless stringed instruments (especially violinists) do one occasion make disparaging comments about fretted instruments (especially guitars and banjos) out of a sense of aggrieved elitism; angry that the popularity they once enjoyed is largely a thing of the past.   The reason I point that out people who hate autotune (like myself) see it as an annoyance. I'm simple self-aware about it and acknowledge that we are a long way from seeing the full extent of the musical/creative potential it can unlock. Autotune was developed as a time saving device. In the old days, singers would have to do multiple takes of a recording to get their performances exactly right, which could take hours. Renting a studio by the hour when you weren't a great singer who could knock out a legendary performance in minimal time made recording a costly endeavor. We perceive autotune as cheating because its corrective AND because it minimizes the time it takes to deliver a vocal performance that would be well within the abilities of a competent singer. We are nowhere near seeing what kinds of things autotune might make possible that would be physically impossible for even the best singers; of seeing autotune transformed from a gimmick into a genuine extension of a singers voice like how amplification came to be an extension of a guitar.

They also fuck with it to make music sound different, like T-Pain does. D'angelo...i love you so much bro. But seriously, all the elements you mentioned with the singing...all have to do with the pitch. if ya pitch ain't correct, it would absolutely sound shitty as hell. That being said, I sing. I don't think autotune is a bad thing at all...I personally prefer low autotune, since it does add a robotic feel, and I do think it takes away from the voice given to me. Pitch is the fundamental thing...if a person is popular because they can't get their pitch correct, and decide to use autotune, then it does feel unfair to people like me who have worked their whole lives to be mindful of the pitch and tone...I don't think what's happening to T-pain is fair, since I do think he has revolutionized Autotune, and Usher saying that was absolutely rude. I think the middle ground would be that the person has a good pitch, and uses autotune for specialized affect...pitch is the fundamental of singing.

People who say he fucked up music obviously don't understand music production or what autotune/melodyne/etc even does. Those plugins aren't going to take a bad singer and make them sound great. As D'angelo said, you'd be extremely hard pressed, especially in pop music, to find a single track or artist that doesn't use some form of pitch correction software (not even mentioning the huge amounts of other processing that goes on to make vocal tracks fit into a mix). Lol I wrote a whole long comment comparing it to an electric vs acoustic guitar before I finished watching the video and saw you used that same example at 12:00. Oops. But yes! That point exactly. Even just with vocals. I'm a renaissance/baroque musician. The conventions, techniques, and the actual music itself are different to a lot of modern music, so my singing wouldn't sound exactly "right" to someone who mainly listens to pop music, and that could be said for any other combinations of genres. But that doesn't mean either are bad. Music doesn't have to be (and shouldn't be!) completely the same or appreciated equally by every single person. That would take all the creativity out of it. Pitch correction is just another tool musicians have at their disposal. It's not inherently 'evil' or whatever. There have always been music purists who think music should be done a certain way, or that other music is wrong (an example comes to mind: tritones were considered the devil's interval! Or in common practice, parallel fifths are a huge no because they were overbearing and intense, but they get used a lot now because they're powerful and compelling), and that's just sad bc it tries to limit all the possibilities out there. There will always be stylistic shifts in music, but that doesn't mean the old styles disappear forever (take it from me, I do music that's hundreds of years old!)
with this and the last vid, im happy Dangelo is bringing back his old aesthetics, I personally was not a fan of the twitch stream videos upload

Honestly this criticism doesn't even make sense to me. Each new song using pitch correction had musicians and engineers making choices to produce it. If an artist made the decision to use autotune in a way that ruins the song, arguably it wasn't "ruined" it was just poorly conceived to begin with. You can't just carve out the part of an artist's style you dislike and go "Oh but that's not their fault that came from T-Pain." That isn't how creativity works.  "Ruined" implies there WAS something there that would have been good sans autotune, that then got forced into a pitch-corrected style that didn't fit the song. Whether that comes from the creator's intent or impositions by producers...T-Pain wasn't standing in the booth with a gun to their heads MAKING them copy him.  It'd be like blaming Basquiat for all the mediocre outsider art that got popular after him: some gallery director still DECIDED to show mediocre paintings; some artist still did the work itself. Maybe their decisions were informed by seeing the success one artist had doing it *right*, but that's hardly causation. You can't really blame someone for other people imitating them.   For real though, what was T-Pain gonna do, send out C&D notices to everyone doing a bad T-Pain impression so his style didn't get a bad name? Artists don't have the power to stop other people from copying them, even if it gives their style a bad name.

I just finished my fourth year of a music degree, which includes music analysis of all genres. My take is that the idea of someone â€œruining musicâ€ is wrong on so many levels. First, itâ€™s flawed to say a single person is responsible in this style. As you said, audio engineers, producers, composers, songwriters, performers, and singers are all involved in the artistic process. Contemporary singers in more popular genres tend to be falsely credited with the entire creation of the song. This both erases more backstage talent and puts a ridiculous amount of responsibility on one person that they canâ€™t control. If I make a good arrangement, the group performing, conductor, original writer, and anyone connected to the potential recording of the piece is also responsible for any potential success. Second, itâ€™s literally impossible to ruin music. While one piece, artist, or artistic movement may gain more popular acclaim, itâ€™s not inherently better than any other. Different strokes for different folks. Just because something isnâ€™t to your taste or focuses on making areas you care about more virtuosic or complex doesnâ€™t mean it objectively has more or less value. So stop hating on people for their art! It all had its place and purpose, and we should value and appreciate all of it, even if we wouldnâ€™t add it to our playlist. D'Angelo has a point about "everything is pitch corrected." As a software engineer who studied EECS (electrical engineering & CS) in university (which includes stuff like digital signal processing that one would use to filter audio), we absolutely could do pitch correction on anything you hear these days, even live stuff, if we really wanted. The delay for using even the heaviest algorithms possible would be no greater than 100ms and that's reaaaaaaaaally pushing it (more like <10ms). I'm not aware of anything that could take that long. And even that amount is imperceptible by humans generally, especially when it's a voice coming out of a speaker on a live stage, which already has considerable delay.

I wish people could see that the heavily auto tuned esthetic is nothing more than an artistic choice. I feel like there is a lack of understanding in the musical process, the way people want their voice heard is a personal choice. If i want my vocals to sound perfect/robotic i will use auto tune/melodine/warping, but if I want raw emotion/empathy/feeling I will always leave the vocal untouched and rely on performance. No matter what, performance always trumps equipment. If someone is bad at singing, a true ear can detect the use of correctional equipment, but does it matter? If the song is good and you like blasting it in your car then the artist has won. Auto tune is nothing more than software. The choice to use it or not is in the artist hands. Listen to what you feel is right, don't criticize others who differ in opinions.

Some people abuse autotune or use it to cover up the fact that they have terrible pitch. That is very noticeable and most people won't like it. Using autotune to make artistic decisions like T-Pain is like putting some extra spice into an already successful meal. It's not better or worse, it's just different. That being said, I know that there are many extremely talented rappers. I may not listen to them, but I can recognize talent when I hear it. It's similar with T-Pain: If somebody doesn't like T-Pain's music, that's fine. It's just important to recognize that he is an objectively talented artist.

In the early 2000s technology and people's access to technology was also changing drastically. I'm finishing up a bachelor's in music production right now, and I can confirm this is 100% true. Pitch correction or autotune is used in any and every genre of music these days, especially since programs like Logic and Ableton (hell even Garage Band) are readily available to anyone who wants to take the time to learn how to use it. Even though some artist require more of it than others, it's the engineer's job to get the "perfect" take, so a lot of times in modern music, what you're actually hearing is something that (visually speaking) is so surgical it's insane - I've been in sessions before where the vocalist and engineer will repeat a phrase 10 times just for the slightest difference in pronunciation for one word, and then mix it into the final product. The simple truth of music production these days is that we want that perfect, first take sound but we still want human elements mixed in, which is why if you listen closely you'll hear the artist taking a breath or so in between sections. T-Pain found a niche in an otherwise oversaturated market, and now it's what he's known for. With how hard it is to break out into the music industry and achieve the amount of success he has, it's commendable more than anything else.

Autotune isn't a bad thing. Not to be confused with tuning someone's voices to make a note sound less flat, it's a tool to make a specific sound, that sliding, unnatural sound. It's a taste, and sure some people won't like it, but it's not like Autotune is a bad thing. What I think a lot of people DONT know is many pop singer's voices are heavily edited (NOT Autotune'd, that is it's own thing) for their albums because there is a specific "pop" sound that is hard for people to naturally accomplish. So their voices are slightly edited to make notes less sharp or flat, but they may not sound as perfect when performing live. It's part of the industry but you don't go around telling all posters that edit/tune their voices untalented or disgraces to music. It's how. It. Is.

I disagree with D'Angelo on one point tho -- pitch IS an important part of singing, because (unless you're just tone deaf, which few people are) pitchy singing is usually a sign of a technique issue, almost always a tension or breath problem. If you have those problems, then that means the "more important" things you talked about like tone quality, clarity, power, are also taking a hit from those technique issues. That's why better trained vocalists tend to have better pitch. Ariana grande has great breath support and like no tension. So she's never pitchy. For a long time Taylor swift struggled with those things which made her pitchy. So it's more of a "bad technique CAUSES bad pitch" issue, and there's not really much room to say that pitch is the least important. If you have all the other important parts covered, pitch will come with it.

Music is an art form.  It shouldn't matter what materials or tools you use to create the art, it's the finished piece that is important.    If you look at a painting,  you don't judge it solely by the choice of brushes,  the kind of easel used,  whether the entire thing was painted with their fingers or a palette knife. You look at how the artist combined the materials and how they used the tools to create an effect that observers can find meaning or enjoyment in.  This doesn't change if the painting is worked in oils, watercolour or acrylics. The effect it has on any individual is also entirely subjective - what looks like a masterpiece to me may  lack beauty or meaning to you.   T-Pain's auto-tuned music has an effect on people. He combines his materials and tools to create art that some people enjoy and some don't. To say that he ruined all other music in the R&B category is assigning him a whole lot of power.  Picasso and other artists created abstract art that some people loved and some people didn't think was real art because the finished pieces don't necessarily accurately represent reality and the world as it actually appears.   The existence of Picasso's abstract art, and the influence he had on other artists, did not stop painters creating new works of classic realism that were enjoyed by people as much as they ever were.    The style of art that people want to hang on their walls may come in and out of fashion,  but a new style coming to popularity doesn't erase all of the other styles of art. People's enjoyment of abstract art doesn't mean they can't also still enjoy realism.   T-Pain may have influenced others to create music using auto-tune the way he did, but that didn't keep more traditional R&B from being made. The use of auto-tune and the intentional distortion of the voice is just as creative, skilled and artistic as the use of an acoustic guitar and someone's bare voice.  The tools and materials chosen may differ but they are both works of musical art that can happily coexist alongside one another under the umbrella of R&B.

"Digitally editing vocals bad" is an evolution of "computer music bad" which in turn is an evolution of "electric guitars bad". Mainstream music is mainstream because a crapton of people like it, and autotune has stuck around because people think it sounds cool.   "More bad RnB music because autotune" is a hilarious example of not seeing the forest because of all of the trees. Autotune is just one of the many ways music production has become more varied, versatile and accessible. Music publishing has also had like, nothing short of a goddamn revolution through the internet and streaming services, social media etc. This has lead to a massive boom in the amount of music published, the variety in music, and accessibility to the average listener. When there's more music in general, there's more bad music in general. Unless T-Pain invented the internet or streaming platforms it seems kind of unreasonable to credit/blame him for any of this.  There's more choice than ever as a listener, and it's kind of funny that people choose to complain about what other people like and listen to in an era of music where it's super easy to choose your own music adventure by handpicking who you want to curate your playlist or just curating one yourself. Auto-tune was invented a year before the Cher song, but that song was the first to use it to distort the voice of the singer. You can't even hear if a song uses Auto-tune, if it is used "correctly". This use of Auto-tune alone is amazing for singers, because they don't need to take a million takes of a song until they get a version where they hit all notes perfectly. It just makes life a little easier like the "smooth lines" option in digital art. Using it like T Pain and Cher is just another audio tool. Like D'Angelo said before it there already was the vocoder that was invented in 1928 and found it's use in music in the 70ies (Mr. Blue Sky by ELO or Autobahn by Kraftwerk are two I can think of) Personaly I also don't like Auto-tune as a way to distort the voice, but people need to understand that their personal taste doesn't mean something is bad.
See for me autotune is like adding a warm filter to a photo to get a vintage looks. Or a guitarist using a pedal to create a different sound and vibe. The guitarist is still putting in the work and is still playing live but there are just certain distorted sounds and feelings you cant hit with a regular guitar and sometimes you need to hit a pedal to get that. Does it make the guitarist less skilled? Does it make them playing live all of a sudden fake? No.

The don't want you to hear it but either the singer is wildly inconsistent and melding together their different takes took a lot more tuning or the engineer isn't that good at their job.  99.999% of the time, if you can hear it, that's a choice. Love the video and agree with everything you pointed out, but just to clarify, 10:57 is a clip of a talkbox. There's no pitch correction involved.  In fact, he's not even singing at all. The way a talkbox works is that tube carries the sound from the synthesizer into his mouth. Then he shapes the sound into vowels, basically turning the synth into his voice. Around this time there were also Vocoders, which achieved similar effects through different methods. Really fascinating techhnology you should look into.

I play a lot in audio engineering studios and I never had the pleasure to work with  pitch modification, but I can say firsthand that everything that goes into any song is incredibly difficult. You write a song (generally just one instrument and a voice with words), you refine it, you find people to play on it, you create all of the other parts, you record it (which the recording process can alone take hours) and then you finally take that recording and prey itâ€™s perfect, you mix each individual instrument so everything fits perfectly in its puzzle, you add the compression and the EQ, delay/pitch mod/reverb/distortion whatever you want. Basically... if you managed to put a song together and recorded you have talent

youtuber Sideways has a really excellent video about autotune and why it's not at all the problem people believe it to be. basically, people use the word "autotune" when they really mean "pitch correction", and pitch correction is used in literally all music production. and it's done so in a way that specifically makes sure listeners won't be able to hear it. like, it's literally just the process of getting multiple vocal takes, and fixing any mistakes by subbing in correct notes from the other takes where the singer didn't mess up. what T-Pain did was more of a stylistic choice ala Daft Punk to give his voice a certain affect. and even if all of this weren't the case, why the hell would you wake a man up out of a sound sleep just to insult him??? and how could anyone defend that???

in my experience working in the music industry where we sell a bunch of music software such as Melodyne 5, Antares: Auto-Tune (auto tune, pitchcorrecting software) Cubase, FL Studio, Pro Tools, etc i feel Melodyne (auto tune software) is like photoshop for a vocalist. it first of all is a tool which can be used for plenty of purposes. it can be used for distortion, it can re-harmonize vocals, and most notoriously, it can correct notes that are maybe out of tune, sometimes you dont want to perform an extra take (recording) since the mixing engineers can fix their voice in post production. its kinda like photoshopping pimples out ya nice picture your fond of. sure you can always wait for your face to clear up, but we live in the future. We have tools that can make the things were not all that fond of go away. but in the wrong hands, the intentions become alittle less noble and way more distorted and uncanny in certain cases.  maybe what usher was trying to say was that there are people who would rather perform music in there natural voice, instead of using Melodyne (autotune) as a crutch to augment and mask their voice. Musicans, singers and artists spend thousands of hours practising and perfecting their sound, honing in on there craft. people who sing opera music cannot rely upon pitch correcting software to achieve a pitch perfect voice, that takes time and dedication. so maybe i could see the trend of augmenting vocals as upsetting to those who practice performing in their natural voice. Because maybe they feel like it discounts their efforts. why practise and try at all if anyone realistically can manufacture a perfect vocal with the right tools?   but what isnt fair in this whole situation is T-Pain being the scapegoat. without realizing, T-Pain bacme an ambassoser for Auto-Tune, and for how modern artists today use autotune today to completely augment and mask there voice. like to a whole new different extent. that just isnt really fair. T-Pain despite being known for his extensive auto tune usage. has a lovely natural voice. T-Pain is a musican, he knows how to play the guitar and piano, and hearing him perform in a live setting proves he can absolutely sing without needing auto tune at all. T-Pain was never at any point hiding his voice in auto tune, He was using it stylistially in his music, he liked how it sounded, so he put himself out there. T-Pain absolutely doesnt deserve any scorn for "ruining the music industry" if you think he does, do some actual research. hes an artist. im sorry that happened to him.
